<h2>All Reviews</h2>

<ol>
    <li> Very nice razor - good weight, and well made.  Balance is good, but for those of us with larger hands, a longer handle might be nice.  Throw away the Derby blades that come with it - they might be good for scraping paint off a window, but don&#x27;t use them on yourself!</li>
    <li> Today was my first ever experience using a double edge safety razor and it won&#x27;t be my last. After years of shaving with Gillette Fusion 5 blade overpriced razors and blades I am happy to say I have been converted after only one shave with the Edwin Jagger. This isn&#x27;t to say I won&#x27;t try different models or brands of double edge razors in the future, just that I am completely satisfied with the double edge razor design. The Edwin Jagger is beautiful in appearance and well designed for use with a nice weight and adequate size. However, the one complaint I have and the reason I decided to rate it four stars instead of five is the grip, or lack thereof. I worried about this before purchasing but many reviewers said it wasn&#x27;t an issue for them. Unfortunately, I found it a little difficult to hold firmly after rinsing due to the handle getting wet. Prior to my first shave with the EJ, I watched a youtube video to learn the proper technique. It turns out that my shaving technique is pretty close to how the video explained to use a double edge. I went with a 30 degree angle with the grain of my beard for the first pass, and against the grain for the second pass. What I noticed immediately was how sharp the blade is and how little pressure I had to apply. I let the razor&#x27;s weight apply the pressure for the most part and simply guided it along its path. I used the Derby blades that came with the razor and have no complaints. I also purchased a thirty pack of Astra blades, which I will try out after my first blade is ready to be changed. My plan is to have my technique down and then try the Feather blades.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I found another model of Edwin Jagger on Amazon that offers a much nicer knurled handle grip judging from the pictures and reviews. It is the Edwin Jagger Kelvin and is an exclusive design for Amazon.</li>
    <li> Thank you very much, great razor, great shaves</li>
    <li> I started to use this razor in Jan 2015. I wipe it clean after each use and it is in a stand. I noticed about 6 weeks after starting to use it that I was getting a rust colored spot on the side. Not it has a full blown rust spot on it and I will have to replace it soon. For the price it should last a while before it starts to rust.</li>
    <li> Great gift for my dad!</li>

    <li> Good quality, no complaints.</li>
    <li> Solid razor, nice hefty weight.. ...and a 3 piece, so the barrel (handle) can be switched out for a different, compatible piece. For about $31.</li>
    <li> Superb craftsmanship! I went from using disposable razors to this with Derby blades (a small package is included when you buy this), and haven&#x27;t been happier. My face has very sensitive skin, and shaving was a daily headache that meant I&#x27;d have razor burn continually if I wanted to be clean shaven.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I thought it was my face being sensitive, but with this razor and the Derby blades I can shave and not have my face burn for the rest of the day.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Plus, the attention to detail is remarkable on this product. Not a blemish in sight. Also, a note about the handle: If you want the completely smooth handle but worry about it being slippery with wet hands I&#x27;d say if you want the smooth handle buy it and you most likely won&#x27;t notice any slipping while shaving. Even with wet and/or mildly soapy hands this one is pretty easy to hold and given the shallow texture of the handle I wouldn&#x27;t imagine the smooth one would be hard to handle.</li>
    <li> If you are new to using traditional safety razors.....BUY THIS RAZOR. For around $30 you will get a very high quality razor. The chrome is high end and well polished. On cheaper safety razors you can see little waves, not on this one.The razor is surprisingly hefty and requires no pressure against the face while shaving. The weight of the razor head resting against your face is plenty. The quality of this item is superior.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In addition to this razor, you should pick the following items:&lt;br /&gt;1. Sample pack of blades. You can get 5-10 different types (100+ blades total) for $20.&lt;br /&gt;2. Proraso pre-shave and shaving soap (green).&lt;br /&gt;3. Badger brush, lather bowl, and stand.&lt;br /&gt;4. Alum bar.</li>

    <li> Has a good feel when in your hand and allows quick shaving similar to a disposable once you get the hang of it. Although this DE razor does not have the highest number of reviews on Amazon, it does get praise from purchasers of other brands who had switched. This was reason I purchased it, and having been my first DE, highly satisfied. Regarding other reviews on &amp;#34;breaking&amp;#34;, I do not see how this is possible unless your using excessive force to tighten down the top. It&#x27;s a simple turn until snug type, not a &amp;#34;grip and vise turn&amp;#34; to secure the blade in place.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Highly recommended.</li>

The razor is solidly built &amp; I have had no problems disasembling are putting back together after cleanups.  Changing razors is simple &amp; easy.  The chrome razor looks great too.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now for the shave itself.  I have never had a smoother face.  This gets so close I would have passed the old credit-card shave inspections in the Marine Corp.  Seriously, my face hasn&#x27;t been this smooth since I was thirteen.  No skin irritation as well.  It&#x27;s everything I could want in a DE razor &amp; I highly recommend.</li>

    <li> I was born in 1946. When I started shaving DE razors were all we had. We did not have YouTube to show us how to use one. Shaving was a daily ritual of nicks, cuts and razor burn. Next came injector razors and we thought we had died and gone to heaven. After that came the double-blade Schick razors and then the three-bladed Mach III.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I used the Mach III for many years and refused to let the manufacturers gouge me even more by going to the 4 and 5 blade razors. So I went back to a DE safety razor. Initially it was the same old story, nicks and razor burn.&lt;br /&gt;Then I went to YouTube and learned how to properly prepare my beard and use a safety razor. Today I get the smoothest, cleanest shaves possible with no nicks or razor burn. They put the Mach III shaves to shame.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I own 11 DE safety razors. This razor has shown itself to be the best. When paired with Astra blades, you can&#x27;t beat it. Astra blades are great. For $34.90 I bought 400 blades from Amazon. You can use a new blade everyday for over a year. It costs more than that to get 16 MACH III blades.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is a great razor.The only thing that would make it better is if it had knurling on the handle like the&lt;br /&gt;Merkur 34C instead of vertical grooves. But putting some alum from an alum block on your hand solves the problem.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Buy it, get Astra blades and go to YouTube to learn how to use a DE razor.&lt;br /&gt;You&#x27;ll never regret it.</li>
    <li> Nice razor, hefty and well balanced.  Keep threads clean and oiled and it should last a lifetime. I see some had issues with the threads corroding out. Just like a straight razor, maintenance is key.</li>
    <li> I decided to make the switch from traditional cartridge to a double edge safety razor. Many people said there is a learning curve associated with the switch but I found that curve to be quite easy to handle.  Within a handful of shaves, I was extremely comfortable with the razor and felt it gave a great shave. The razor is very rugged and the blade is super easy to change. My only suggestion would be to buy a case for the razor.  Overall, it is the perfect fit for me and I couldn&#x27;t be happier with the performance and ease of use.</li>

I always start with the grain of my hair.  This was a little tricky, because I am so used to  the straight razor cutting exactly where I see the blade touch. Lastly, was the against the grain pass.  I was a little leery of this because I was never able to do this with regular cartridge razors because it would tear up my face, leaving  razor burn, in grown hairs, and general discomfort.  This little puppy popped those hairs off with hardly any feeling!  Afterward I rinsed with cold water, applied some after-shave lotion  and voila, wet shaving perfection! For those who say that this razor slides when you grip it, wtf?  This has not slipped once since I&#x27;ve been shaving, and I use anything but a vice-like grip.    Just nice and gentle does the trick, and it has never slipped.  How about the reviews about the weight being in the handle and not the head and having to push too hard?  Also poppycock (always wanted to use that word).   Sure most of the weight is in the handle, but the head of this razor is still perfectly acceptable to get a great shave, and it&#x27;s only $35!  So, in closing, after re-reading this novel I just wrote, this is a fantastic razor.  It comes with 5 Derby blades, and you get two sides to each of those blades, so you are well supplied  with razors for a while.  I would recommend this item to anyone who is looking for a great, comfortable shave.  And not just the men, my wife used this to shave her legs last night, and man! Better than I imagined.  As others have undoubtedly learned, shaving is a process that can&#x27;t be rushed.  Please take the time to develop a good pre-shave routine and don&#x27;t be afraid to experiment with different blades to find one that works best for you.  While many shave forums are frequented by those obsessed with the closest shave possible, use videos on shaving to get more accurate and more practical advice.  Avoid making extra passes and avoid the 3-pass shave.  It is well advised to only shave with-the-grain and cross grain.  Never shave against the grain. It causes ingrown hairs, increases irritation, and increases the likelihood of infection.  And remember one more thing: make not shaving part of your shaving routine.  If possible, skip a day.  This will allow your face to heal a bit and allow any irritation to quiet down.  It also improves the skin for the next round of shaving.  Enjoy your shave.  Please let me know if this helps. The heft is pretty weighty in the hand, but it is extremely well balanced.  This concerned me a bit.   The foremost thought was that it would be too heavy to properly shave with.   After all, I am coming from the world of disposable razor cartridges (Mach 3).  Secondly, I was struck by the craftsmanship.   The fit to my hand is just right in a normal shaving grip, upside down, and cross-face orientations.   Viewed from any angle the chrome finish is gorgeous, and although the handle is chromed it is textured with a lined pattern so it stays grippy even wet or when shaving cream is on your fingers.  You might think that the only thing that could make it better would be if it were a butterfly-type head, but when it comes to dependability and resistance to wear and tear I&#x27;ll take the Edwin Jagger&#x27;s simple screw-on method versus one that has moving parts any day of the week.    Without any sort of \\&quot;purchaser bias\\&quot;, I can honestly say the razor performs superbly.   My typical shave is in the shower with no mirror, so I jumped right into it with my new double edge safety razor.  This might seem scary to some, but with practice you&#x27;ll know the contours of your face by using your touch to check for missed spots.  I admit, even with years of no-mirror shaving, that I was a little nervous.  The end result of the first shave was excellent!  It was all baby butt smooth, no nicks, and just a 1/2\\&quot; circular spot of razor burn (went away by mid-day), which wouldn&#x27;t have happened butI held the handle too loosely on a tricky part.    Economy was another consideration I had when making the switch.  Let&#x27;s see, a Gillette Fusion 16 pack for $41.25 or Derby DE Razorblades 30Ct for $5?  No contest!   In a very short amount of time, in fact the first time you need another package of cartridges, the Gillette becomes much more costly.  As time goes on the division of value gets even larger.       A quick piece of advice: be confident!   More nicks will happen from your uncertainty than anything else.   Just be aware that what you&#x27;re holding is many times sharper than cartridge razors and to treat it accordingly.   Two weeks in of daily shaving and I haven&#x27;t had any nicks or cuts.  Also, be sure to change the blade when you start to notice a less smooth shave.   There is no proscribed time other than ~4ish days, but it can vary, based on your facial hair.   Some people have lots of hair that is soft, so they can go 5 or 6 days.  I don&#x27;t have that much, but each individual hair is very course and thick so I replace the blade at the beginning of every 5th day.  While others have a ton of course thick hair and need to replace the beginning of the 4th day.    Quick summary: I couldn&#x27;t be happier with this purchase.  I&#x27;ve got a great looking piece of kit that gives me a smooth shave every time.  Plus, traveling around to other countries is infinitely more simple with the Edwin Jagger than a cartridge razor.  You can always find DE razor blades around at extremely cheap prices, compared to the hassle of finding the right cartridge for your handle or the need of buying another handle with cartridges because they don&#x27;t carry what you need.</li>

    <li> This is my first DE razor, and I have been using it for a couple months now.  It has worked excellently, and is beautifully smooth and shiny as an added bonus.  At first it does feel as if the handle is a little short, but one quickly realizes that no additional length is needed, or even particularly desirable.  I have tried it with Feathers, Derbys, Sharks, and Bluebirds, and my conclusion is that the blade makes all the difference in the world as to the success of the shave, but the razor not so much (although the weight does actually help with the shave). (BTW, I also bought a Parker 22R DE razor and used it as a comparison to the Edwin Jagger.)  My conclusions about the blades are: 1) The Feathers can last up to 20-25 shaves per blade but are dangerously sharp and WILL draw blood frequently on the first several shaves, 2) The Derbys are very forgiving but are usually done after about 4-5 shaves, 3) The Sharks are a little sharper than the Derbys, but still fairly forgiving and DEFINITELY last longer, up to 6-7 shaves per blade, and 4) The Bluebirds seem largely indistinguishable from the Derbys, but might be just a little sharper initially.  I have decided to standardize on the Sharks, and at about $0.18 per blade per week the long-term savings will be quite substantial.    So, get this razor, get a good shave cream/soap/oil (I like Proraso and Speick), maybe a good shaving cream brush, and give it a try!</li>

The Razor--  The EJ DE89L razor deserves every one of the 5-stars I gave it.  Top quality construction, well designed, I expect it will last a lifetime.    I&#x27;m new to double-edged (DE) shaving and I&#x27;m glad I chose this razor for learning.  It is a \\&quot;medium aggressive\\&quot; razor, not so mild that you don&#x27;t get a good shave, yet not so aggressive that you have to use a lot of care.  More experienced DE shavers say it is not only good for learning, I won&#x27;t \\&quot;outgrow\\&quot; it.    If you do any research at all on this razor, you&#x27;ll find that it is the \\&quot;go to\\&quot; razor these days.  You&#x27;ll also hear/read about guys praising the chrome plating.  It is very well done.  I was worried at first that they were enamored with this razor just because of its looks, but it is equally good at shaving.    Edwin Jagger is an English company, from Sheffield.  The razor&#x27;s head is made in Germany, under a joint venture with Muhle, a German company.  It is a 3-piece razor.  The handle, the base, and the cap are all separate pieces. This makes it easy to clean.  Changing blades is a bit \\&quot;fiddly\\&quot; at first, but I think I could do it now with my eyes closed.  The secret is to turn the razor upside down.  I typically flip it and rest the cap on a towel, unscrew the handle, then flip the cap over to let the base and blade drop off.  Then I reverse the process with a new blade.  Some have complained about the short handle.  For me it was more of adjusting to this razor after using long handles on  cartridge razors.  However, technique is different for the two types of razors.  With the cartridge razors I tended to grasp the whole handle.  To keep from using too much pressure with a DE, most guys just hold it with the tips for their first three fingers.  Using thatgrip there is plenty of room, even enough to vary my grip--near the tip, at the balance point, or near the top.  Also, I haven&#x27;t had a problem with the handle being slippery, unless it gets lather on it.  You can also wet your fingers on an alum block for extra grip if you feel you need it (an alum block is good to have anyway).  Traditional Shaving--  I&#x27;m very glad I switched to traditional shaving.  There is a learning curve, but I&#x27;m now getting shaves that are closer than I was getting with either the electric or multi-blade razors. My skin is much healthier looking, and no rashes or bumps. I do get a little razor burn, but as I get better, there is less and less, and it usually disappears by noon.  I see the day coming when it will be the exception.  As for the healthier looking skin, I&#x27;ve heard mass-market shaving foam is hard on it.  I can think of no other reason why there would be such a difference.  I will also save enough money on blades in the first 6 months to pay off my brush, the razor, and blades.  DE blades are typically less than $.50 apiece, some less then $.20 per blade.  If you decide to switch to DE shaving, I recommend learning about it first.  The technique is very different from using a cartridge razor.  There is a wealth of information on the shaving forums.  Badger and Blade is a good one (badgerandblade.com).  Check out their Wiki.  There are also excellent instructional videos on YouTube produced by both \\&quot;Mantic59\\&quot; and \\&quot;Geofatboy.\\&quot;  Blades--  I  recommend you buy a sampler pack of blades to learn on.  Get a pack with at least five different types of blades.  The Derby blades that come with this razor work for some people, but they are too mild for my beard.  When you get the sampler pack,  work through them using at least two blades of each type until you find one that seems to work the best for you.  If you choose this route -- enjoy!!  Edit:  I&#x27;ve been using this razor now for four months and I&#x27;m still happy with it.  Razor burn is minimal now, and when it happens, I know what I did wrong.  I mentioned above that my skin is improving.  I get compliments now on how nice my skin looks, from people who have no idea that I shave DE.  Not bad for a middle-aged guy.  My routine is to use a man&#x27;s face-wash, shave with traditional soap, rinse with Thayers Witch Hazel, use Nivea after-shave balm (when the weather&#x27;s cold and dry).  I&#x27;ve always used a face-wash and the Nivea in cold weather.  The only thing I changed was the way I shave and I added the Witch Hazel.</li>
    <li> I bought this razor as I was looking for quality that will last a lifetime. I&#x27;ve not used the Merkur brand yet although I plan to add one (#34C) of those too. Comparing the Edwin Jagger to my old Schick Kronas is night and day difference. The Jagger is quality made, fit and finish, and simply put is a precision instrument. The 5 Derby blades that come with it are head and shoulders above the trash blades I picked up at the local pharmacy and they align perfectly in the razor. The Derby blades are available for around $15/200 on Amazon so will also be ordering those. The razor itself has nice weight that glides across your face. If you let it do the work rather than pressing it into your skin, you will have no problems with irritation or cuts. Patience is a virtue. My beard is heavy/coarse and I&#x27;ve yet to find a disposable cartridge razor that comes close to the cut I get using the Jagger.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m not sure what all the fuss is about in the reviews about people using a double edge razor and complaining of cutting themselves. It&#x27;s like anything else, use care and pay attention to what you are doing and you will get an expert shave without irritation or nicks on your face. Preparation is key. Start with a wash cloth soaked in hot water placed across the beard/face. After repeating this process several times, wet your face then lather it up using circular motion with a badger brush. Start with short downward strokes with the grain of your beard not putting pressure on the razor but rather, let the weight of the razor do the work for you. Rinse the razor often. Afterwards, rinse your face with cold water to close the pores and then apply your favorite after-shave or balm.</li>
    <li> The finish on this razor is simply amazing. This is like looking at a beautifully chromed Harley Davidson. If I never used it for shaving, I would frame it and hang it on the wall.  But I do shave with it. It is the smoothest shaving razor in my stable of 10 razors. It does not \\&quot;bite\\&quot; you if you have an occasional lapse of technique like other more \\&quot;aggressive\\&quot; razors might, yet it rewards you with a smooth shave. I am always happy with the shave I get and how smoothly the razor performed.  It&#x27;s a perfect razor for the DE (double edge) beginner, but seasoned DE veterans also appreciate its performance.  And have I mentioned how amazing the finish looks? :)  It&#x27;s nicely balanced and feels comfortable in your hand while using it.  When I first looked at the handle, I thought it might be a little slippery when wet, but I&#x27;ve had no problems at all using the DE89L  with wet hands.  I rotate the DE razors I use each day, because I&#x27;m a DE fanatic, but if I was forced at gunpoint to pick one razor to use every day, the DE89L would be my choice.</li>

It&#x27;s chroming is deep, flawless, and bright.  The chroming method used is the same used by Rolls Royce for its chrome accents.  The Edwin Jagger De89 comes with either a vertically lined handle, or a smooth handle.  I went with the lined as I thought it might provide a little extra traction with wet hands.  The razor arrived in a nice, blue, textured presentation box (however, the box did get a little crushed during shipping.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The razor itself is an absolute joy to use. It also heats up as you rinse it and retains that heat, which felt great against my skin.  After just a few, careful shaves, I already felt very confident with the use of the razor.  The shaves are wonderfully close (as good as any I&#x27;ve ever had), and the little red bumps on my lower neck that I always assumed I&#x27;d have forever have begun to fade (believe it or not, a DE razor is much kinder to your face).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As for blades, I recommend ordering a sample pack, as different blades act and react differently with every face.  It&#x27;s just another customizable aspect of DE Shaving. The shaves are amazingly smooth, and while not as \\&quot;aggressive\\&quot; as some of my other razors, it gives just as close a shave.  When I finally got a Merkur I was very disappointed in its finish.  Merkurs are the most popular new DE razors sold, and I guess I was expecting more.  Don&#x27;t get me wrong, they&#x27;re fine razors, but they come with little scratches and tool marks that slightly mar the finish.  The Edwin Jagger, with its perfect plating and great shaving-characteristics just makes me happy every time I pick it up.umps on my lower neck that I always assumed I&#x27;d have forever have begun to fade (believe it or not, a DE razor is much kinder to your face).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As for blades, I recommend ordering a sample pack, as different blades act and react differently with every face.     <li> The quality of this item doesn&#x27;t come into question. The chrome plating is top notch, and it&#x27;s got a nice heft to it.     Why only two stars then? The design is HORRENDOUS. The handle is a mere three inches long. Even for not so large hands like mine, it&#x27;s a pain to hold comfortably, and requires an arthritis inducing grip.     What&#x27;s worse, instead of a decent grip pattern embedded into the handle to make it easy to hold while wet, the handle only has vertical ridges in it.     It won&#x27;t twist in your hand, but if you don&#x27;t keep a vise-tight grip on it, it will slide up and down while you&#x27;re shaving, leading to an aching hand or nicks and cuts... or both.     Worse still, instead of the classic butterfly style opening to replace the blade, the entire head comes off and has to be opened to remove and insert blades. Sooner or later, you&#x27;re going to end up slicing your fingers trying to replace a blade.     And keep in mind, a safety razor cuts with a shallower angle than modern cartridge razor blades.You can&#x27;t get away with the shave-and-dash with a safety razor, the way you might with a multi-blade cartridge razor.  You&#x27;ll want to use some sort of oil/cream base on your beard before lathering up, to help the blade glide, and definitely a moisturizing aftershave to help with all the scraped skin when you&#x27;re done.     If you&#x27;re going to go with an old fashioned safety razor, I would recommend trying this one: [[ASIN:B003NTHWLU Parker 99R Butterfly Open Double Edge Safety Razor &amp; 10 Shark Super Chrome Blades - Heavyweight + Long Handle!]] Long handle, textured grip, and an easy open butterfly head. Everything I wish I&#x27;d gotten with this razor.</li>

    <li> I got this razor in mid-May as an early Father&#x27;s Day gift (I was too impatient to wait &#x27;til June). I have used it at least twice a week since then. My previous razors have been the Gillette Mach 3 and Fusion, so that is my basis of comparison.    First, let me tell you that this does NOT shave any closer or more comfortably than the Gillette razors...at least not in my experience. I will say it shaves about as close as the Gillettes, but not closer. You can also expect to spend about 10-12 minutes shaving, so you aren&#x27;t saving any time.     There is a steep learning curve with a double edge safety razor. The first several times you use it you will probably regret buying it. My first shave was close, but since I didn&#x27;t have the technique mastered I cut my self in no less than 15 places. The water I rinsed my face with was a nice pink shade from all the blood it was washing off! While it got better, it took me about 4 or 5 weeks of uncomfortable shaves before I figured it out. I have since learned that you need to put ABSOLUTELY NO PRESSURE ON THE RAZOR! Simply hold it against your face and let its weight guide it as it falls down the surface of your face. Moral of the story: don&#x27;t get discouraged at first.    The reason the shave takes about 10-12 minutes is because you really need to shave three times to get the job done correctly. My first pass is with the grain. The second pass is across the grain. The third pass is against the grain at about a 45 degree angle (not directly against the grain). After that I do small touch up work, mostly under my chin and around my adams apple. There are numerous videos on YouTube showing how to shave with one of these.    Even though it takes a while to shave and it isn&#x27;t any more comfortable than the Gillette razors, I absolutely love this razor...now that I know how to use it. There&#x27;s a certain nostalgic feel to it and for the first time in years I actually look forward to shaving. It makes me feel more like a man. I also have much less skin irritation afterwards. When I was shaving with a Gillette I would usually have several white heads on my chin the next day. I haven&#x27;t had a single one since I started using this razor (even when I was hacking up my face). Also, the area at the top of my neck remains a normal skin tone, rather than that irritated reddish skin tone.    I&#x27;m also surprised at how long one blade lasts. I&#x27;m on blade #3 of the original pack of 5 that came with it, and I&#x27;ve been using this razor for just over two months. Where I was spending around $50/year on blade replacements for the Gillette, I should be spending about $5 a year on replacement blades for this razor.    If you have the patience to figure this thing out and don&#x27;t mind spending a little more time shaving, then I would definitely recommend getting one. Otherwise you&#x27;re better off sticking with the Gillette or Schick.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve always had rough hair on my face, and I&#x27;ve always had difficulty with getting a close shave. I had read about DE shaving for a while, and I finally decided to try it out. If you&#x27;re looking for the best razor, I would suggest this one. It&#x27;s the only one I&#x27;ve tried, but it also tends to get the highest reviews on shaving sites, or at the very least is even with the Merkur. Some guys seem to naturally get smooth faces every time they shave, and it looks like they don&#x27;t grow any hair. Men like me must have more testosterone, because my hair refuses to go without a fight, and it always grows back quickly with a vengeance. I just couldn&#x27;t get a smooth shave with my Mach 3, but everything changed when I got my Edwin Jagger.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The razor itself is very pretty. The pictures don&#x27;t do it justice. If you&#x27;ve never used one before it&#x27;s a little confusing how to put the blade in when you first pick this up, but once you realize that the top two pieces screw off, it&#x27;s as simple as it can get. It&#x27;s not at all difficult to hold the razor or to use it, the only difficulty is getting the angle right when drawing down along your face. Even this isn&#x27;t especially hard to figure out though, and after a few shaves you&#x27;ll have it down. The blade moves very easily across my face, and it never tugs on me like cartridge blades do. I&#x27;ve tried two blade brands so far: Derby and Wilkinson. Derby is much less aggressive and is very easy to start with. These blades come with the razor in a pack of five. I bought some Wilkinson blades, and they&#x27;re actually quite nice, but far more sharp.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I should note that you do not apply pressure when shaving with DE razors. Doing so will only get you cut. This takes some practice to get used to, but you&#x27;ll learn quickly. The best way to get a close shave is by first going with the grain, then across it, and then lightly against it. It&#x27;s also important to get some shaving soap and a brush. It lathers up very nicely, and can make a big difference in how smoothly the blade cuts. It is also important to unscrew the razor and dry it off after shaving. This will keep your razor clean and make it last indefinitely. I usually dry mine off and then let it sit on a towel to get rid of any residual moisture. It still looks like the day I got it, so I must be doing something right.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I recently grew my beard for about a month and a half, and had more hair on my face than ever. I shaved using my Edwin Jagger with a Wilkinson blade, and had no tug or pull. The hair came off quickly. Oddly enough, going from the most hair I&#x27;d ever had I ended up with the closest shave I&#x27;ve ever had. Four and a half days later and my fast growing facial hair looks like it&#x27;s just a day or two after using a cartridge razor. One of the best parts about using DE razors is the price of blades. They&#x27;re incredibly cheap, especially in bulk. Cartridge razors dulled pretty fast for me, and using a weak blade would just irritate my face. These blades not only last longer, but they&#x27;re so cheap you can toss them out after every shave if you feel like it. (You won&#x27;t need to, especially for quick daily shaves, but it&#x27;s nice to have the option to switch out whenever you want.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I am extremely satisfied with this razor, and if you&#x27;re looking for one to buy, go with this one. It gets great reviews, and I have nothing negative to say about it. It&#x27;s everything I hoped it would be. It feels manly and professional, has very cheap blades, is easy to handle, and is incredibly easy to dry out and take care of.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Ultimately:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Razor itself is perfect, no issues at all, probably the best option currently out there for new or experienced users.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Derby blades: very cheap, very easy to use. Not as sharp as other brands, not as close of a shave&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Wilkinson blades: still pretty cheap, much sharper and aggressive than Derbys, gets a much closer shave, a little more difficult to use</li>

    <li> Initial review Sep 2013: The chrome finish is flawless and it looks great, however the manufacturing tolerances are substandard. While the razor does lock the blade in a fixed position there is a significant amount of play that allows the blade to be out of alignment with the shaving head when locked down.  If you are not very careful when tightening down the head the blade will be at an angle. You need to look closely, carefully position the blade, hold it in place and carefully tighten with the handle. The blade locator pins have some taper for alignment but not enough.  Once I am able to get it fully closed with the blade straight, I am otherwise happy with the shave it delivers. If the blade alignment were not an issue I would rate it 5-stars. The loose blade fit is tiresome, I did expect more based on the number of 5-star reviews.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Updated Jan 2014: The loose blade fit has been determined to be due to the blades: particularly Derby and Merkur.  Switching to Gillette Silver Blue and Feather I found a tight fit with no loose fit and alignment problems.  For me the Derby and Merkur are poor blades compared to the Silver Blue and Feather.</li>

    <li> The razor is a 3 piece razor.  It has a handle, and a two piece head.  The razor goes between the two head pieces, and everything is held firmly together when you screw the handle to the head.  The handle is just the right length.  The barrel has lines in it which makes it less slippery when wet.  The head is heavy, which is good.  The weight of the razor is all you need to shave--there is no need to apply pressure.  It has a great feel.  It is not adjustable, which is a good thing in my mind,  as there is nothing to get gunked up with leftover soap/hair, and I couldn&#x27;t imagine wanting to adjust it anyway.  Clean-up is a breeze.  Safety demands that you give your full attention when changing blades--they are DE razor blades, after all.  But once changed, it is a very safe razor.    I am able to achieve a baby smooth shave (BSS) in 2 or 3 passes, using [[ASIN:B0022R947O Feather Hi-Stainless Platimum Double Edge Razor Blades]].  The gap between the razor edge and razor housing is perfect.  The shave is a little more aggressive than the much more expensive [[ASIN:B0046JVV6S Feather All Stainless Steel Double Edge Safety Razor]], which takes 3-4 passes due to its less aggressive bite, and costs 6 times as much.  Note:  Feather makes razor blades and razors.  The feather razor blades and the Edwin Jagger razor are a better combination, in my view, than the Feather razor/feather razor blades.    I should note that I did have a problem with the first Edwin Jagger I received from Amazon.  The blade edge did not line up with the head&#x27;s edge, which is not good, and causes nicks.  Since I only have a sample of two to go on, I don&#x27;t know if this is a quality control issue, or if the first razor I received was the only defective unit--but you should probably check blade alignment before you shave.    In any event, Amazon has an excellent return policy, and they sent another one out with no push-back whatsoever, and paid for the return postage to boot.  What more could you ask for?    The most amazing thing about this Edwin Jagger DE 89LBL razor is that I am able to get a better shave from it than the much more expensive feather stainless still razor, which is 6 times the cost of this razor.    Do a search on \\&quot;geofatboy Edwin Jagger Chrome\\&quot; to find a video review/demonstration of the non-lined handle version of this razor. I did not like them as much as the Feather blades I already have, so I am saving them for emergency backup. These, and an old coffee mug are all you need to open a new and very enjoyable horizon.</li>

    <li> Like many others new to double edge shaving, I was trying to decide which razor to begin with. After much deliberation, I chose the Edwin Jagger DE89Llb. Now, I have read that everyone&#x27;s face is different, every razor and every blade work differently together, what works for one may be awful for another. I give it two stars only because it obviously works well for others, and you can tell it is well made.     - --    One more thing: the EJ is slightly lighter than the Merkur 34c, but a big issue is that more than half the weight is in the handle.     <li> Ok, so here&#x27;s the deal,&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I live this razor.  Its my first attempt at a DE safety razor which I purchased based off of previous reviews.  One thing that attracted me to it was that based on other reviews its not that &amp;#34;aggressive&amp;#34; of a razor.  Meaning, I suppose, that the blade isnt as exposed as some others leaving room for error.  I should however mention that this razor can still mess you up! Badly! If you&#x27;re not careful.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let me break it down for you:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1)  If you have never used a Safety Razor, do your research or you&#x27;re gonna have a bad time.  You DO NOT shave with this thing like you do with a cartridge razor.  It will look like a scene from a horror movie if you do.  Saving with a razor like this takes A LOT more time than you are used to with a a cartridge razor.  Shaving with a Safety Razor is in of itself its own Art form.  You must first master the basic techniques of shaving with one at the same time really learning the intricacies of your own face.  PLEASE do your reaserch before going full hipster!  If not you WILL regret it.  I recommend a forum like this  http://www.reddit.com/r/wicked_edge/&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2) Blades make probably the biggest difference by far.  I have only tried two different types so far.  The Derby blades that come with it are for me alright but not the best.  I did find the shave close but not impressive.  I ordered the Feather blades which were absoloutly amazing.  The cost of the Feather blades are much higher than many of the others but no where close to the cost of a Gillete cartridge, so we are still saving lots of money.  Find a buddy or three that want to get into this with you, each of you order different types of blades and give them a try.  Your skin type, hair type, etc all have an impact.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3)  Purchase a pre shave cleanser such as Glycerin soap.  Some say its not important but I personally have had wonderful results.  Also, DO NOT use some crappy shaving foam or gel.  Get a proper shaving soap or lotion to do the deed.  See, problem is, when you get that nonsensical foam, it creates a thick layer that you spend a number of shaving strokes just to get to the base of your hair follicle.  All the while creating irritation.  A nice shaving soap lubricates very nicely and you are in closer contact with the skin.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4)  I need to reiterate.  Technique is everything.  It takes some time to get good.  I must admit I am in the process of doing just that.  I rushed my shave the other day and boy did I regret that.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Have fun with it, get good, take your time and you will have the closest, most satisfying, least irritating shave you have ever had.per shaving soap or lotion to do the deed.     <li> I ordered a DE89Lbl from Amazon Warehouse Deals that was described as being in Like New condition. I figured maybe it was a return and that at the very worst it would have water spots and one of the 5 included Derby blades might be missing. But there were no water spots and all the blades were there, but I immediately noticed that the bottom of the screw on the part of the head that screws into the handle was shorn off. This was obvious because unlike the rest of the razor, it was not shiny chrome but dull, jagged metal. I shook the handle and heard rattling. It looked as if the broken off piece of screw was in the handle, and sure enough I was able to spin it out of the threads in the handle with the tip of a toothpick.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I took a photo of the shorn off screw under an illuminated magnifier so you can see what I&#x27;m talking about.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A number of reviewers have had bad luck with this razor because of this screw. In some cases this screw sustained damaged as a result of the razor being dropped. It&#x27;s possible that the razor I received was dropped by a previous buyer, who then returned it. Of course there are certain objects one should avoid dropping at all costs, such as fountain pens and expensive double edge razors. But a tool designed to hold a blade used for shaving shouldn&#x27;t be that delicate or fragile, should it?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve also read on Amazon and elsewhere about DE89 owners who say that the screw eventually rusted.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;And, it&#x27;s possible the screw on the razor I received broke due to the handle being over tightened. If you visit Edwin Jagger, then go to safety razors, then follow the link to order online, you are taken to The English Shaving Company of Sheffield, where this warning appears in the listing for this razor: &amp;#34;Warning: Do not overtighten the DE head. Cast metal is fragile if dropped.&amp;#34;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I own three one-piece design double edge butterfly type safety razors that I inherited from my late father. All are Gillettes, and all were manufactured in the US in the sixties or seventies. They are solid tools built to last a lifetime or longer. I don&#x27;t know if my dad ever dropped any (knowing him, he probably did), but I doubt a single drop would suffice to damage one to the point of rendering it unusable. Because I have those, I don&#x27;t really need a new DE razor, but I&#x27;m eager to try a good quality safety razor of a type that is being manufactured today. The DE89 comes very highly recommended and I don&#x27;t doubt that it deserves the many 5-star reviews it receives, but the fact that it is built with a cast metal screw that apparently breaks pretty easily is for me a real deal breaker. The one I purchased from Amazon Warehouse Deals that was listed in Like New condition was marked down to nearly twenty bucks, and I can&#x27;t imagine paying over thirty for something so fragile.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Why buy a razor that you may have to baby and that, unlike the aforementioned older Gillettes, does not seem built to last a lifetime or more? To protect the cast metal screw from rust, you might have to disassemble the razor after every use and dry it. You will have to be careful to never ever overtighten the handle. And of course you must never drop the razor. I don&#x27;t see the latter as a terribly significant problem because as I say, you don&#x27;t want to ever drop a fountain pen either, not to mention glassware, cellphones, babies, etc. But that cast metal screw is clearly a problem with this razor (and maybe three-piece* safety razors in general) and although I&#x27;m disappointed that I received a DE89 with a broken screw, I think I may actually be lucky, because it would be worse if it arrived undamaged only to break in after the return grace period was past. I contacted Amazon about the problem with the DE89 I received and they sent me a prepaid return label and are giving me a full refund. *(Butterfly safety razors, which are sometimes called TTO razors for twist-to-open, are one-piece, the DE89 razors arethree-piece, and there are two-piece safety razors that are similar to the three-piece except that the bottom part of the head doesn&#x27;t separate from the handle. For more info see the article at Shaving 101 titled, &amp;#34;Types of Safety Razors.&amp;#34;)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m probably going to order a Merkur 34C two-piece safety razor and see how that goes. It gets great reviews and is often compared favorably to the DE89 - in fact most reviews that compare them put the 34C ahead of the DE89 - and it won the About dot com Readers’ Choice Award for &amp;#34;World&#x27;s Best Razor&amp;#34; in 2011 and 2013 (e.g., see &amp;#34;The Ultimate Guide to Merkur Safety Razors&amp;#34; at Mister Shaver). It&#x27;s sometimes called by different names, such as the Hefty Classic or the Merkur HD (for Heavy Duty). Based on what I&#x27;ve read, it sounds as if it may be as well-built and durable as some vintage razors.similar to the three-piece except that the bottom part of the head doesn&#x27;t separate from the handle. For more info see the article at Shaving 101 titled, &amp;#34;Types of Safety Razors.&amp;#34;)  I&#x27;m probably going to order a Merkur 34C two-piece safety razor and see how that goes. I use short,slow,deliberate strokes with only enough pressure to engage the blade to the beard. I have to say that I definitely have gotten a closer shave than with my old Atra  twin cartridges or three blade disposables. I&#x27;ve read people saying they have to shave twice to get a close shave. I would say twice around the jaw line but otherwise once is close enough. It takes me no longer to shave with this DE razor than with my old Atra cartridge razor. Of course this razor will last a lifetime but you will want to take it apart after each shave and dry it after rinsing thoroughly, reassemble razor but don&#x27;t retighten just leave a little \\&quot;play\\&quot; until next use, this will allow the razor to dry thoroughly and not corrode the razor. This razor cost me a little under $40 but I figured with the price of a pack of 6 multiblade cartridges being around $20 this razor easily pays for itself after using a pack of 10 DE blades at less than $2.     <li> I just wanted to put my $.02 worth in.  I found that when I 1st started doing de shaving the reviews helped, so here is what I have found.  1st, I was using the multi-blade cartridge type razors before I switched over to the double-edged razor.  Like most people I changed over due to the ridiculous expense of the cartridges.  I started out using a Parker 98r butterfly type.  With this I was using a brush that I had which I later found out was a boar bristle.  I was also using the store shaving soap.  The 1st discovery I made was that switching over to a badger bristle brush made a tremendous difference.  I am using the tweezerman brush and it works really well I have not had any significant issues with bristles falling out.  I also have been experimenting with different soaps.  I have used the Taylor of old Bond Street, head slick shavings cream, the gel in the can of different varieties and even regular soap.  As far as blades I have used the shark, Derby extra, feather, Wilkinson and even the drugstore variety.  I tried to give everything a fair evaluation and here is what I have found.  As far as brushes, there is no question that the badger brush works better than the boar bristle.  As far as the blades I find that the Derby extra is the best \\&quot;happy medium\\&quot;.  The feather blades are sharp but don&#x27;t be fooled by some of the reports, you are not going to be performing surgery.  They are sharp but it&#x27;s a razor blade it supposed to be sharp.  As far as the razor, I was not sure if there really would be any difference but I have to say that the Edwin Jagger de89lbl makes a huge difference.  It holds the blade at a better angle and the cut is less aggressive but still does a better job..  I rarely have to use a styptic pencil and the amount of 5 o&#x27;clock shadow is significantly less.  As far as soaps I have found that the head slick shave cream works the best for me.  I do not even mix it in a shaving cup.  I just wet the bristles shake out the excess water and then putabout 2 peas worth on the brush and that&#x27;s enough to do 2 well lathered passes and even the 3rd if you need to.  It is mentholated so if you do not like menthol you might not like this.  If that is the case the Taylor of old Bond Street is a close 2nd.  I have a fairly course beard and I must shave every day.&lt;br /&gt;So for what it&#x27;s worth: Edwin Jagger de89lbl razor, tweezerman badger bristle brush and head slick shaving cream.  This seems to be the best combination for me and if you are looking for your 1st entry into double-edged shaving, I think this would be an excellent starting off point.  Once you get your technique down you will find that double-edged shaving is actually much more gentle to your face than those expensive cartridges and does a better job for a lot less money.</li>

    <li> I don&#x27;t have much else to add to the reviews of this great razor other than to make sure to have the blade put in correctly. The top and bottom pieces of the guard, or the part that sandwiches the blade, should both curve inward (toward the blade). They will grip the blade firmly when you screw in the handle, so you don&#x27;t get any razor wobble. Otherwise you&#x27;ll carve your face up. That may sound self-evident to you experienced wet shavers, but if you&#x27;ve never really messed around with a classic-style safety razor, like I hadn&#x27;t, then it may not be immediately obvious how it&#x27;s supposed to go together. Hope this helps another novice.</li>

    <li> Double edge razors are having a revival in the last few years, and it&#x27;s because they&#x27;re simply better and simpler for shaving. I use mine in the shower, no need for shaving foam or any other nonsense. Just wet your face up, make sure you have a relatively new blade, get the proper angle, and slide it down. No need for extreme pressure, just use the weight. No need for shaving foam, but you can if you want. I disassemble it to let it dry, and each blade lasts me at least a week of shaving every day. That&#x27;s 10c/week, compare to disposable razors, or the hilariously unnecessary multi-edge disposables and cartridges, or the unclose shave of an electric. Best option out there.</li>

    <li> Initial quality seems very good. Chrome plating is much better looking than on a Merkur. But it really isn&#x27;t well constructed. It&#x27;s made of pot metal that rots from the inside out and can easily break. Lasts only a few years. Up to 10 if you&#x27;re lucky.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Also the 3 piece design is a bit annoying to load. There are twist to open razors but they have a lot of fragile little mechanical parts that are exposed. In general double edge razors are not well designed. Both because of their loading mechanism, their paper thin blade that flexes/vibrates as it&#x27;s cutting leading to easy weepers, the blade sits at a 45 degree angle at the skin so it scrapes hairs off and not cuts. Because of this they can tug and blade life is much reduced so that even with two edges blade life is less than half of a single edge/injector razor (which only uses one cutting side). Trust me I&#x27;ve used a double edge for years before discovering better options. They are just inferior razors that are wrongly designed. Get a single edge, injector, or a straight razor.</li>
    <li> This is my second DE razor. After my fist cheaper one started rusting I turned to the forums on badgerandblade.com for recommendations on which razor to purchase and this one was the most recommended.     <li> I first started out with the much advertised multi-blade disposable razors such as the Mach III Turbo and Gillette Fusion during my teen years. I then transitioned to an electric razor for ease of shaving and to save time during my late teen/early 20s. Both cases I&#x27;ve experienced razor burn. After doing some research on the old-fashion ways of shaving, I decided to see what they have to offer.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After researching the different DE safety razors on Amazon I am pleased with my purchase of my first DE safety razor.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I followed some of the directions from the instruction booklet and from the internet and tried to tailor it to how I would incorporate it into my normal routine. I first started by washing my face with Dr. Bonner&#x27;s castille soap followed by 3 hot towel presses with hot tap water. I then generously applied coconut oil to my face. From what I heard online and now from experience, coconut oil does soak into the skin. So if it takes a while to get to the next shaving area, I noticed for myself that I&#x27;d have to reapply coconut oil to that area. This I can deal with because I&#x27;d rather not add chemicals into my body through my skin. Once finished I rinsed my face with cold water and dried my shaver with a microfiber cloth. So far no razor burn :)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One thing to note with coconut oil, there is a slight build-up inside the razor assembly. Aside from the care instructions mentioning to ensure to it out, I recommend wiping/drying with a cloth.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Even though this is my first DE safety razor:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Pros:&lt;br /&gt;-Great weight&lt;br /&gt;-Bundled razors worked well for me.&lt;br /&gt;-Nice look and finish&lt;br /&gt;-No razor burn&lt;br /&gt;-Solid construction&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons:&lt;br /&gt;-A little time consuming (practice should help with that)&lt;br /&gt;-Not a butterfly open (for quick easy access...from what I&#x27;ve seen)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I hope this review has helped you in your search for a DE safety razor. I&#x27;ve used it to shave my head about 5 times now, my face a little less,  and have not cut myself once. In fact, when I use aftershave to seal the deal, there is little or no sting. I just get a better shave, period. It was used for the most part 6 days a week other than when he broke his arm and it was not used for around 2 months. Tonight after shaving he went to clean it and when he went to put it back together the head would not thread onto the handle as though the threads were striped. He inspected it, threads are still present but they appear that the sharper outer edges are gone. Almost as though either the handles male threads were originally cut under size ot the heads female threads were cut oversize. The handle was never tightened hard just lightly when being reassembled. Looks as though it is a victim of poor quality control. Time to look at other manufactures, with the simplicity of the design this should be a razor that can be passed down to future generations but this one is not.  Update 1/25/17, finally decided on new razor. His new HONE 15 arrived. This one IS solid CNC machined brass. Definitely a lot higher quality. Way different price point than Edwin Jagger.     <li> Had been using an electric shaver for years after making the switch from expensive multi blade cartridges.     <li> I had been looking at getting into the DE wet-shaving crowd for awhile, but was hesitant due to the people saying it was so slow, you will cut yourself, expensive, etc etc. This was up for sale for $23 and decided it was the time to bite.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Out of the Box&lt;br /&gt;--------------&lt;br /&gt;The razor is a lot heaver than you would expect. I thought it would be light and about the size of a standard \\&quot;Fuzion\\&quot; razor I have been using. However, this thing is dense (you can tell it&#x27;s solid metal), and short. More on these later.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Razor Install&lt;br /&gt;-------------&lt;br /&gt;Razor install could not be easier. Lay the razor head flat on the edge of the table and spin the handle counter clock wise. Stand the razor head on it&#x27;s top and lay the razor in. Place the bottom of the head on the top, and place the handle back on spinning clockwise. After it&#x27;s somewhat tightened, lay it flat on the edge again to turn clockwise until tightened. This was you are never really touching the head and will avoid being cut.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Shave&lt;br /&gt;-----&lt;br /&gt;Take your time especially your first time. I only had three nicks. One was when I wasn&#x27;t paying attention and poked myself with the corner of the razor. The other two were small bumps that I got on my third pass against the grain. Either of those could have happened with a standard cartridge, so I&#x27;m not really counting them.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It really didn&#x27;t take me as long as I thought it would. I went in being paranoid thinking I would slice my face up the first time after all the horror stories. If you have half a brain then you shouldn&#x27;t have any problems with this. I had been letting my hair grown out for about two weeks and this cut right through it like butter. The cartridge razor couldn&#x27;t get more than a couple CM without being clogged.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Method&lt;br /&gt;------&lt;br /&gt;Hold the razor at an angle. Just start with it barely angled and increase the angle till you find that sweet spot. It only takes a few seconds to find this. I chose towork in areas since I had a good two weeks of growth. After that I could lather up my whole face and do it without worrying about it drying out.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All in all the shave took barely any longer than the standard cartridge. The extra time it took to build lather was the main cause of this. The razor cut with one pass as good as the cartridge does after a couple so that equals out the extra time it took by me going slowly (to prevent cuts).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Conclusion&lt;br /&gt;----------&lt;br /&gt;Don&#x27;t be afraid of the blade. Go into it with respect knowing you have a sharp blade to your face, but that it&#x27;s up to you to control it. I had no problems right out of the gate. I didn&#x27;t have any cuts and the shave went well.</li>

    <li> I have to start with this:  The first time I used this razor, [[ASIN:B002QTX8WU Edwin Jagger Double Edge (DE) Safety Razor - Lined Chrome Handle]], I wanted to run outside and ask complete strangers -- women -- to feel how soft and smooth my face was.  Yes, it was that good and beats all other razors I&#x27;ve used, bar none.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The razor comes packaged in its own box, along with a starter set of five (5) Derby Extra blades.  When I removed the razor from the box, it was beautiful and shiny, with not one nick anywhere on the razor.  It had a weight to it that I was unaccustomed to, having grown up shaving with all the Gillette rip-off cartridge razors from the mid-1970s through part of July of 2012, but it felt just right when I held it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The razor disassembles to change the blade.  You unscrew the handle from the head and the two finely machined pieces that hold the blade easily separate.  The bottom of the head assembly has two small nubs whose purpose is to position the blade properly in the razor&#x27;s head when you reassemble the razor.  When the blade is seated properly and you reassemble the razor, the blade is held snugly in place with no wiggle room whatsoever.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I think this design is superior to the design my father used, with the twist mechanism at the bottom of the handle.  I think the twist design doesn&#x27;t allow a blade to be held as securely and loosens more easily than razor that screws together like this one.  In fact, I think that&#x27;s one reason men who had nothing to shave with but safety razors nearly always drove to work with little pieces of tissue paper on their faces, to soak up blood.  I think another reason for razor cuts back in the day was due to older manufacturing techniques.  I&#x27;m sure the factories that churn out double-edge razor blades have more exacting measurements and tolerances now than they did 40+ years ago.  I also think there were poorer shaving creams available then, too, than there are now.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If youread about how to properly shave with a safety razor, you will have no issues with the razor or the blade.  You let the weight of the razor head do all the work.  Voila!  When you run into trouble and your face looks like it was on the losing end of a cat fight, your blade might be too dull, you might be putting too much pressure on the razor head to try to get a closer shave or you&#x27;re doing something else that&#x27;s causing you to have a bad shaving experience.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A word of warning... Do not admire the luster of your razor by running your finger over the top of the razor when you have a blade loaded in it. (Did I mention Gillette&#x27;s shaving products, especially its cartridges, are huuuuge rip-offs?)  The one thing I have to do is be very careful shaving around my nose.  One misstep and I need a neck tourniquet for even a minor trespass into the tender areas near and around my nose.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I learned that cutting beard hair is not the major contributor to dulling a blade that many think it is.  It&#x27;s the mineral buildup on blades from the water left on the razor.  After shaving, I wipe down my razor with a towel and then blow-dry the blade to ensure it&#x27;s dry.  My first blade, which was also my previous DE blade, lasted for six weeks or so, give or take a week.  Granted, since my beard is white, I can get away with not always having to shave every day.  However, cleaning and drying a blade after each use definitely prolongs its life.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This razor truly is a display of craftsmanship.     <li> I like this razor, but there&#x27;s a big caveat of which you should be aware.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I had to sell this because I discovered that I had a skin allergy to chrome/nickel. The EJ is made from \\&quot;pot metal\\&quot; which is cheap, low grade metal and is given a coating of chrome which contains nickel. After shaving with it for a bit, I noticed that I was getting bumps on my neck and cheeks; not weepers (i.e., ingrown hairs), just bumps.  I didn&#x27;t get them with my all stainless steel razor or my antique Gillette NEW.  I realized eventually that it was the nickel in the chrome plating that was giving me skin dermatitis when using the EJ.  So, while this is a very good razor, you should stay away from it and other chrome plated types (such as Merkur, etc.) if you have an allergy to nickel or chrome.  For me, I&#x27;m sticking with an all stainless steel razor.</li>

    <li> My Jagger razor is probably more heavily chromed than my Merkur. It is a nice looking implement, both are.  I took it for a test tour of my face today and did not get nicked. I&#x27;ve been shaving with a double edge blade for the last month or so, so I&#x27;ve probably re-learned how to use one. Used one for three or four years then started looking for an easier way when I was 19.  I&#x27;ve tried electrics several times. Usually quit using them because I would have to touch up areas with a blade anyway. They do not shave as close as a blade and if you use a pre-electric potion you pretty much have to wash it off, negating the &#x27;dry shave&#x27; convenience of the electrics. I&#x27;ve used many of the disposables and multi-blade razors. They do make it easy. They do make it pricey. Back in 1984 I think, Gillette had a shave cream dispenser with a built-in brush. I tried a couple of them with not much reason to continue. I bought a brush and some cheap Williams hard soap at the drugstore. Didn&#x27;t work too well. I might be the only person who bought two of them.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you don&#x27;t have one, get a brush to use with the Jagger. I bought a Tweezerman here for under ten bucks. It has badger bristles and works well.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Something I read somewhere really works well for me. I put the shave brush in very hot water in a coffee mug. While it&#x27;s marinating I wash my face. Then shake the water off the brush and dump the water out of the coffee mug, put just enough hot water to cover the bottom of the mug back in, as hot as you can get it. Swirl the brush tips around about a quarter-sized amount of shaving cream in the mug, I&#x27;ve been using Proraso. Then fill your lavatory  a little more than half full with the hottest water you can. Put the mug with the brush and shaving cream in the hot water in the lavatory. You can still run hot water on your razor if you want or just swish it around in the lavatory hot water on the side not occupied by the mug/soap/brush (you don&#x27;t want water from the sink slopping into the mug and diluting the soap). The nice thing is, rather than risk slicing or abrading your face, when you want to go over an area again you just take the brush out of the cup. The shaving cream will be very warm. If you keep doing that, keeping shaving soap on your face before going over an area, and paying attention to what you&#x27;re doing you can shave blood free, cheaper and probably closer than with the expensive cartridges. If you are thinking about switching from those to a DE and decide to keep using the multi-blade cartridges, you should still consider the brush-soap-cup-in-the-sink  tactic.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update 10/20/12&lt;br /&gt;I bought another one of these after my brother saw mine when he visited the other day. He has been duly warned that there is a (fairly short) learning curve. The razor, as with the first one, shipped fast and free. You can&#x27;t beat these people to do business with. Can&#x27;t say I won&#x27;t end up buying a third one of these, if I buy a fourth, I&#x27;ve got a problem. Nice product. Nice people to buy from.</li>
    <li> First, I&#x27;m 64 years old, I know dougle edge razors, I&#x27;m also a woman. I purchased this razor for my husband. He is bedridden, and I have to do the shaving for him.     <li> I must admit that despite being an avid Amazon customer for almost as long as it has been in business, I have never posted a review for any of the products. Admittedly, this is my first DE, but it certainly won&#x27;t be my last as I have a bit of the collector bug for things I enjoy - and that word is key.  You see, I have never enjoyed shaving.  To me, it has been akin to cutting the grass - a never-ending cycle of drudgery that more often than not resulted in skin irritation and ingrown hairs.  I accepted this through the years as part of the process until I started getting that smattering of salt-and-pepper in my beard.  With the seeming change of coarseness of my facial hair as I have aged, the irritation and frequency of ingrown hairs increased to an almost intolerable state.  I have been fortunate to have been able to work from home quite a bit over the last year, thus the frequency of shaving decreased enough to let my neck heal a bit between shaves.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Of course, through all this torture I had been using any of the latest and greatest eleventy-billion bladed leviathan that I thought might be the holy grail of shaving for me.  Little did I know the answer was much more simple and low-tech.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Just a few weeks ago, I scheduled a flight to the home office to meet the new CIO. Quite an important face-to-face for me.  As luck would have it, I shaved with my latest failed experiment and the result was the absolute WORST irritation and ingrown hair that I have ever experienced.  It was so bad, I hated to go out in public.  During one of my Brazilian Jiu Jitsu matches, I tapped not because of the choke was set in deep, but because the abrasion on the ingrown hair was horrifically painful (I have quitea high pain tolerance at that).  I began to fear that the ingrown hair was so severe that it might keep me looking like a mutant on my trip, and that was not a good first impression for me to leave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After reading several forums filled with men that had the same problem, almost all resolved their issues by going back to what their fathers and grandfathers used in lieu of the latest cartridge razors.  More research prompted me to purchase the Edwin Jagger De89lbl along with the [[ASIN:B004L4EING Van Der Hagen Men&#x27;s Luxury, Shave Set]] as this was touted as a good mid-priced DE setup for beginners.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here I am two weeks later and my face is almost back to normal.  I am back to shaving at least every other day with the Edwin Jagger.  Not only is my face much less prone to irritation, but I have found that I enjoy the ritual - the \\&quot;ME\\&quot; time.  Shaving almost seems therapeutic in a sense.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My wife and child were terrified that I would cut myself the first time out, but I followed some of the other reviews of this particular DE, and it&#x27;s true; the weight is sufficient therefore DO NOT apply pressure.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Certainly, I still have more to learn regarding the art of shaving, but this product provided me with a good price entry point and a set of training wheels.  In addition, my neck no longer looks like inspiration for a new villain in an X-Men comic.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you are having problems with bumps and ingrown hairs, don&#x27;t take forever to try DE shaving like I did.</li>

To avoid cutting yourself when changing blades, pinch it in-line longways with your thumb and forefinger on he top and bottom of the head when the razor is dry and not soapy and twist the handle CCW. Don&#x27;t over-torque it when you tighten it down. After you shave, loosen the head the same way, rinse it under the sink, then blow the water out and hang it to dry.     <li> Yesterday I received my new Edwin Jagger DE89lbl from Amazon. I really wanted to like this razor. It appeared to be perfect. As I stand there checking blade position and admiring the construction of this razor, IT HAPPENED. I suddenly became aware that in order to use this torture device, I would have to place that very sharp, very exposed blade against my bare skin. I became VERY apprehensive. I do not have baby smooth skin, nor is it soft and supple. After building a smooth creamy lather in my bowl, applying Noxema to the area to be shaved, and  thoroughly covering my chin with lather, I was ready. With shaky hands, I picked up my Edwin Jagger DE89lbl and laid it gently against my face. Holding back my tears, I let gravity pull the razor toward the Earth as I attempted to maintain the correct angle of the handle. The gentle scraping sound of the razor cutting the hairs on my face reassured me I was doing it at least partially correct.  As I looked in the mirror, i could see a clean strip of skin where shaving cream had once been. I looked for signs of incisions, abrasions, inflammation, irritation, aggravation OR BLOOD. Nothing. Nada. Zip. I had done it. I proceded to shave my entire face with the grain. Not a nick. I relathered and shaved against the grain...Again not a problem.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Looking back, I was kinda not manly worrying about removing layers of skin on my face.     <li> After owning this razor for 10 months, here are my conclusions.  I still use my Edwin Jagger DE razor every day.  When I first got it, there was a learning curve of about a month.  I was cutting up my face quite a bit at first before I got the hang of it, but it was worth it.  Every time I shave with it, I shave down one time, sideways one time and up to finish off (with the exception of my neck with I only shave down twice on to eliminate irritation).  I started off using the Parker Safety Razor 100% Black Badger Bristle Shaving Brush along with the Derby DE razor blades and Taylor of Old Bond Street Sandalwood Shaving Cream.  This worked well, but took more time when you considered that you have to clean the brush every time you use it.  I have since switched to using Nivea for Men Q10 Energy Shaving Gel which is the best shaving cream I have ever used and does just as good a job without the brush.  If you haven&#x27;t used this shaving cream, give it a try.  It gives you a nice, thick lather and has a neutral smell--great stuff.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;While the Edwin Jagger gives me a very close shave, there are some issues.  It is tough to get a really close shave directly under the chin (not as close as with Mach 3), on the adam&#x27;s apple area (easy to cut yourself) and on the top of the beard just below the nose (leaves just a pinch of stubble that is just hard to get with this razor).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A big reason I switched to a DE razor was to save on the ridiculous cost of the Gillette Mach 3 blades.  The Derby DE blades are 7.5 cents each and the Mach 3 blades range from $1.38 (the best I&#x27;ve found) to the $2.50 range per blade.  I used to get roughly 1 1/2 to 2 weeks out of the Mach 3 blades when I was just shaving downwards only one time.  I get 3 full shaves (shaving 3 different directions) out of each Derby blade and I could get four, but what&#x27;s the point in pushing it with dull blades at all when they are 7.5 cents each?  They stay sharp for three shaves shaving three directions.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Coming back to the problems above with the Edwin Jagger DE razor, I still use my Mach 3 for getting the stubble directly under my nose, directly under the chin (shaving up) and on my adam&#x27;s apple area (no more cuts).  Since I have been doing this, I have totally avoided cuts and get a perfect shave.  And by the way, I have tried all of the tricks to using DE blades that I found on youtube videos.  I still think the Mach 3 is better for certain things.  I would say that now my Mach 3 blades last 3-4 weeks per blade, so I&#x27;m still saving a lot and I&#x27;m getting a much better shave then when I was previously shaving down only with the Mach 3.  I do believe that razors and blades have improved over the years since Gillette has taken over, but the positives improvements don&#x27;t justify the insanely higher cost of the blades.  By using the Mach 3 with the Edwin Jagger DE razor, I get the benefits of the newer technology (which means less cuts and a better shave on the curves of the face) while still saving a ton on my blades since they last longer.  Also, I end up with a far superior shave since I am making 3 passes over my beard.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In case you are wondering, I have an average beard with dark stubble.  When I used to to just shave down with my Mach 3, I had a nice 5 o&#x27;clock shadow at the end of the day.  The way I am doing it now, I would say my shave lasts at least twice as long as it used to and I no longer have a 5 o&#x27;clock shadow at the end of the day.  One last thing.  Try out Bump Patrol aftershave treatment if you have any issues with those annoying red bumps on your neck.  The stuff works wonders.</li>

    <li> This is my second Jagger (got one to keep in my travel kit rather than swap back and forth) but rather than just add to the kudos for the excellent Jagger razors, here&#x27;s a nifty modification:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You may find after becoming familiar with this fine razor that you&#x27;d like a bit more aggressive shave than the mid range exposure of these. This increases the blade gap slightly and will give you a more aggressive shave.     <li> I&#x27;ll keep this short and sweet so you&#x27;ll quickly know the reason behind the epic failure of this razor.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This was my first foray into safety razor territory after having become fed up with the constant change and rising cost of the cartridge style razors. As mentioned, I wasn&#x27;t using it more than 2 or 3 times per week. I was obviously over tightening the head, but didn&#x27;t realize. Thus rendering the razor completely useless.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You&#x27;ll just have to take my word for it that I was not applying some serious torque when tightening up the razor head.
