Overall, I definitely recommend this razor to someone looking for a better shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Advice:&lt;br /&gt;There are a TON of different blades out there, and they do make a difference. I personally like the &amp;#34;Shark&amp;#34; blades because they&#x27;re uber sharp and I have crazy thick facial hair. I would suggest buying a variety pack of blades along with this razor if you haven&#x27;t used a safety razor before. Also, invest in a shave set (soap and a brush). The soap, to me, is way better and cheaper than any cream you&#x27;re going to buy at Wal-Mart. As far as using the razor... It require MINIMAL pressure to shave with. Let the weight of the razor do the work, or you&#x27;ll be bleeding like a stuck pig. Watch a tutorial or read up on proper safety razor shaving before diving in. It will save you skin, and make you way happier with your purchase.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;PROS:&lt;br /&gt;Durable&lt;br /&gt;Provides a GREAT shave with the proper blade and technique&lt;br /&gt;Manly&lt;br /&gt;way cheaper than replacing the blades on your electric or &amp;#34;reusable&amp;#34; razaors&lt;br /&gt;Solid, heavy feel&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons:&lt;br /&gt;The handle is a little shorter than you may be expecting (may the length of a deck of cards)... but I knew this when I bought it&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It takes a little getting used to.... As I mentioned above, learn how to use this thing before hacking up your face and neck. There are some great tutorials online</li>
    <li> Very nice looking double-edged razor and does a great job.</li>
    <li> This razor is made by a well known and reputable company. The razor looks nice and seems to be made very well. I&#x27;ve had some really nice shaves with this razor and have zero regrets. Enjoy!</li>
    <li> Razor reviews should be viewed as subjective, the &amp;#34;my razor is better than your razor&amp;#34; types of reviews hold NO credibility on certain &amp;#34;facts&amp;#34; alone - with that in mind, here is my experience.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Fit and finish is perfect, weight of handle to head ratio feels good in the hand and allows the head and blade to do the work as you just use your hand to tilt slightly and guide the razor direction.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The design has lines, or raised curved ridges running in parallel with the handle that allows you to have a firm grip on the razor - I know this as I am one arm / hand handicapped at the moment and have NO problems at all just using the one hand to hold, and rotate as necessary the razor in just the one hand with out having to lay it down and re-position my grip.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This model has a closed comb at the safety bar, this makes it a little less &amp;#34;aggressive&amp;#34; - in that less of the blade is open and exposed and applied directly to your skin.  All features of size, weight, comb, aggressive or not need to be paired to your face contour and whisker direction, density, and coarseness.  There is no such thing as one size fits all, or one that is better than any other because of a persons individual body and hair characteristics.  This can make trial and error a bit expensive using just the razor, or swapping out with a replacement handle to change weight ratios and length.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Knowing all of this, I choice this model based on quality, features, and to some extent pricing.  I was looking for a bit more tame, or less aggressive razor and opted to experiment with finding a perfect match of razor to face by testing different blades - also rated for sharpness and &amp;#34;aggressiveness&amp;#34; .&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As with razors, the blades themselves will be subjective as to the comfort and closeness they provide - again based on your face and whisker textures.  I found the supplied Derby brand of blades that came with the razor to not be a match for my face, I am switching over to the Personna blades, and may tweak to the Crystal brand if necessary.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have a more than modest neck scar (in a crease line) that I need to pay attention to while shaving, the closed comb of this razor has served me well in that.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My suggestions:  Use a less aggressive razor, and tune in an aggressive blade unless you already know your whisker coarseness rivals that of sandpaper where an open comb safety bar would be better suited.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is a three piece razor, I wish they had a two piece with the same features and handle length, and head weight, they do not, I knew that, and am not deducting any stars for that.  I do deduct one star for one reason, the DE blades supplied stick out (on the non-shaving sides) past the head dome and deck.  Though they do not pose a real hazard to your face or other body parts while shaving, they do make holding the head and handle for disassembly a hazard to your fingers tips if and as holding the head by the side edges.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I recommend this razor if it fits your needs, quality, features, pricing are all there - give it try.my face, I am switching over to the Personna blades, and may tweak to the Crystal brand if necessary.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have a more than modest neck scar (in a crease line) that I need to pay attention to while shaving, the closed comb of this razor has served me well in that.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My suggestions:  Use a less aggressive razor, and tune in an aggressive blade unless you already know your whisker coarseness rivals that of sandpaper where an open comb safety bar would be better suited.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is a three piece razor, I wish they had a two piece with the same features and handle length, and head weight, they do not, I knew that, and am not deducting any stars for that.     <li> I had originally switched from a cartridge razor to a straight razor due to the amount of painful irritation I would get on my face, which would last all day, as well as the poor shave I got that required me to re-shave several times in order to meet uniform standards, which made my face even worse. The problem with the straight razor was that in order to not slice my throat, shaving took a very long time. While I preferred the straight razor over the cartridge, I didn&#x27;t always have that time in the mornings, so I found myself using the cartridge razor again.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Enter the safety razor. This razor has a solid weight at the head that requires you to put zero pressure in order to shave, (nor should you, heads up). With slow, short strokes, it glides across the skin, getting an incredibly close shave in the process. There is a learning curve, as you learn to stop putting pressure on the razor head, and to angle it so the razor is just barely touching your skin, but after a few days to a week the shave quality will be comparable to a professional straight razor shave in a barber shop. At the same time, you will find that your shave time has been reduced back down to nearly the same as when you were using a cartridge razor. All that for a better shave, with far less irritation.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;During the learning period, you will slice yourself. Same as when you first learned to shave with the cartridge. Don&#x27;t be discouraged, you will learn quickly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Derby blades it comes with are good blades, but you may have to experiment with different blades to find the ideal one for your skin sensitivity and beard. I have very sensitive skin and a very thick beard, a terrible combination, and this combined with a simple moisturizing shaving soap bar and a drug store aftershave have completely eliminated my irritation. The good thing is the blades are cheap, especially compared to cartridge shaving, so this razor will shave you a lot of money in the long run. I was using Gillette Fusion cartridges before I got this... The difference in price between the replacement razors meant the safety razor paid for itself by my second pack of blades. Add in the savings with a long lasting shave soap vs the toxic canned stuff, and switching to safety razor wet shaving will put several more dollars in your wallet every month.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Finally, the razor itself is resistant to rusting, so you don&#x27;t have to worry so much about that - Yet another big plus over my straight razor.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, this is a very well crafted razor that combined with a decent shave soap, (I use the Van Der Hagen Deluxe soap, and got the Van Der Hagen Luxury Shave Set, all very cheap) and a proper wet shaving method will save you time, money, and irritation on your face. Definitely recommend for yourself, or as a gift.</li>

    <li> After researching DE razors for a while, I decided to buy the Edwin Jagger over the more popular Merkur.&lt;br /&gt;The choice was mainly due to the price of the EJ being lower than Merkur, and EJ came with it&#x27;s own good set of reviews by users. I dont know. )&lt;br /&gt;In any case, I bought the model that had ridge lines to provide whatever little grip it can provide.&lt;br /&gt;Other than the constant slipping issue and how careful I need to be so as not to have a deep nick on my jaw, I am thoroughly pleased with my purchase.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Derby Blades:&lt;br /&gt;This purchase came with free 5 Derby blades, and I am so thankful they decided to ship them free to be tried out.&lt;br /&gt;After using it, I realized that I will never buy a Derby blade again.&lt;br /&gt;It is very rough on my skin, and doesn&#x27;t feel sharp enough. They last longerthan the Derby&#x27;s for sure.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Shaving Technique:&lt;br /&gt;The first thing I noticed when I shaved with this razor, is how forgiving the Gillete Mach 3 or razors of it&#x27;s ilk are.&lt;br /&gt;You cannot use the same strokes and methods that you did with your Gillettes or Schicks when you are using a DE razor.&lt;br /&gt;You have to use very short strokes, and you should NOT press into your skin.  You can stretch your skin using your other hand, and gently glide the DE razor in short strokes.  Go with the grain and not against it.&lt;br /&gt;Once you are done, do an encore, even though you think you look &#x27;clean shaven&#x27;.  You will not regret it.&lt;br /&gt;After the second shave, you will look shaven in a way you probably haven&#x27;t seen yourself, if you used a Mach 3 or whatever.     <li> I really like this razor, the weight of it feels really right in my hand.  But I was beginning to wonder how many different blades I&#x27;d have to try before I found one that really worked well.  Trying to find a perfect blade (brand) for my particular razor, shaving style, skill, face... It looked to be a long process.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;However, I noticed one day last week that my not having tightened the handle completely changed the shave quality of the blade I was using.  For the better.  So I decided too try it (loosening the handle) deliberately, and found that it changed the shave quite a bit.  The problems were, of course, the very limited adjustment range, and that loosening the handle even slightly allowed the head assembly to rotate.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So I visited the plumbing repair aisle of my local home store and bought a box of #36 o-rings, which seemed about the right size.  They were, and fitting one over the threaded post between the head assembly and the handle allowed me to adjust the pressure on the blade while preventing the head assembly from turning. The o-ring cushions and holds the handle firmly, and allows for a range of clamping pressure and head height.  Tightening or loosening the handle changes the performance of the razor, as expected.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I don&#x27;t know if it&#x27;s true of all razors, but this razor has a circular inset where the handle meets the lower head assembly.  The o-ring pretty much disappears into it, with just a thin black line showing at minimum pressure.  It looks designed and intentional, which is nice.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I bought a sampler of blades when I bought the razor, and in my initial survey I found that their performance varied from ineffective to hazardous.  With the o-ring in place the aggressiveness of the blade can be increased, but not decreased.  The less effective blades work better, with all but the least effective becoming quite usable.  The hazardous blades got worse.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My hypothesis is that the gap height, blade angle (resulting from the curvature) and leading edge position determine how well a given blade works with a given razor.  Looking closely with a magnifying glass I can see that tightening the handle from first contact to maximum pressure causes the blade curvature and angle to increase while at the same time decreasing the amount of blade exposed (slightly) and the vertical gap between the edge and the lower head assembly (quite a bit).  Blade stiffness also seems to increase, but I don&#x27;t have a way of measuring that.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Try it!  And let me know if it works for you.  I&#x27;m very curious to hear whether it works for other people.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Davee (resulting from the curvature) and leading edge position determine how well a given blade works with a given razor.  Looking closely with a magnifying glass I can see that tightening the handle from first contact to maximum pressure causes the blade curvature and angle to increase while at the same time decreasing the amount of blade exposed (slightly) and the vertical gap between the edge and the lower head assembly (quite a bit).  Blade stiffness also seems to increase, but I don&#x27;t have a way of measuring that.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Try it!  And let me know if it works for you.  I&#x27;m very curious to hear whether it works for other people.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Dave</li>

    <li> This is a great razor.  I was torn between both this and the Merkur 34c and ordered both.  I tried cancelling the Merkur about five minutes after I placed the order but I got the \\&quot;no guarantee of cancellation\\&quot; message and they shipped it anyway.  I did send the Merkur back and had to pay return shipping for it and I wasn&#x27;t happy about it but that&#x27;s another story.    Anyway, I got this and I&#x27;m very happy with my purchase.  It&#x27;s well balanced, along with being very easy to assemble and disassemble. It&#x27;s a three piece razor, which just means that you unscrew the handle and the other two pieces come apart so you can insert a new blade.  This doesn&#x27;t mean that the razor is cheap, it&#x27;s just that some razors are two piece (with the little screw that turns to separate the top like wings, so you can put in a new blade) or three piece.  In truth, I prefer a three piece because you want to keep the razor and razor blades clean, so it&#x27;s easier to clean up.    If you&#x27;re new to shaving with a double edged razor, let me tell you that a decent razor and compatible blades for you are essential to having a good, nick and cut free shave.  You might think that a razor is a razor, so why not just spend $5 or $10 on a cheap one? Well, that&#x27;s what I did initially and I regretted it.  I bought a cheap, $4 DE piece of junk and feather blades.  I looked like a horror show afterward, because of all of the nicks, cuts and blood.    So, what&#x27;s the difference?  Well, the cheapie had a big gap between the guard and the blade and there was no adjustment or alignment possible. From there, I got the feather blades.  Feather blades are generally accepted to be the sharpest DE razor blades out there.  Trust me, this is a recipe for disaster and that&#x27;s exactly how I cut myself up so bad - a razor with a large space gap, the sharpest blades I could find and my inexperience.    The EJ89 is different.  Aside from being a beautiful razor, it&#x27;s weighted very nicely and easy to control.  The gap between theguard and the blade is much smaller and the razor is aligned well. The advantage in having a lesser amount of blade exposure means that you will get a good shave but that it&#x27;s more forgiving in the fact that if you make a mistake, you either won&#x27;t cut yourself or you won&#x27;t cut yourself as bad.    If you&#x27;re converting over from using a cartridge razor, expect a small learning curve of about two or three weeks. When you&#x27;re shaving with a cartridge, like a fusion razor, you&#x27;re likely used to putting more pressure on the the razor and the blade to get a close shave and not worrying about cutting yourself.  With a DE razor, you can&#x27;t do this.  You don&#x27;t need really need to put pressure on the razor, you simply need to guide it and let the weight of the razor and the blade do the cutting.    The blades: these are every bit as important as the razor.    Derby blades:  A great blade to try or start with. They give an excellent shave, aren&#x27;t nasty sharp and I&#x27;d say they&#x27;re somewhat forgiving when it comes to errors.    Feather blades: If you like the idea of samurai sharp steel pressing against your face, so you can look like a blood sacrifice or someone who is trying to commit harakiri starting from your face down, these are the ones to go with.  I mean, you can try them in the future, just take my advice and don&#x27;t make them the first blade you start with.  You don&#x27;t have to have THE sharpest blade out there to get a smooth shave.  You can get a smooth shave with all of them without having to look like ritual death.    Treet blades: I like these.  They&#x27;re very sharp but not too sharp to cause a lot of nicks and cuts.  I get a great, smooth shave without any problem at all.  These are my preference.    Quite honestly, order a sampler pack of blades so you can experiment and see which blades work best for you.    Last, let me point out how cost effective shaving with a DE razor is: If you buy blades in bulk by the 100 or 200 pack, whether here or elsewhere, you can get those100-200 blades for the price it would cost you (or less) to buy a single 8 or 12 pack of Mach 5 Fusion blades.</li>

    <li> If youre looking at this review, it probaly means you are researching wet shaving and wondering which of the 2 razors always mentioned for beginners to choose - you should actually put down your money on.  Having owned both of these super popular and recommended razors I will provide the absolutely immediately noticeable difference.  As objectively as I can, here is the comparison of these 2 wildly talked about/recommend \\&quot;industry standard\\&quot; razors.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Merkur is the more aggressive razor, actually it&#x27;s rather noticeable (although still considered a mild/beginner razor)&lt;br /&gt;EJ is the much more forgiving razor and smoother (and the \\&quot;prettier\\&quot;, \\&quot;shiny\\&quot;, aesthetcially pleasing razor as people keep commenting).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Merkur is a much smaller/skinnier razor (the 34c which most people get.. come with a much heavier/thicker handle) and has a MUCH better grip (with the knerling pattern and \\&quot;ring\\&quot; near the bottom of the handle).&lt;br /&gt;EJ is chrome-plated and much smoother and aesthetically \\&quot;wow\\&quot;.  The hanlde is much wider and a bit longer, but the grip can easily become challenging if handle or fingers get semi slippery.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Shave:&lt;br /&gt;I found the Merkur to be very noticeably aggressive and thus much more susceptible to discomfort and irritableness of skin. (but read on on my &#x27;ultimate lessons\\&quot; regarding all this below).  Most will tell you \\&quot;the more aggressive, the closer the shave possible\\&quot; and yeah theoretically i can&#x27;t argue.. EXCEPT.... the EJ hands down gives you a smoother, closer shave from my experience (my latest test was to use both during the same head/face shave.. using the same blade... with the Merkur getting the fresh Feathers blade and the EJ having gone through a full set of shaves that i end up typically having to toss out the blade when using Feathers).  Hands down the EJ was much smoother, needed less clean-up time to get there, and felt much more comfortable throughout.  I ended up using the EJ to clean-up the Merkur side (b/c the Merkur side was just becoming too uncomfy and raw on my head).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The one advantage of EJ i&#x27;ve come to think of having read all the reviews is... the EJ head is somehow holding the razor just a bit better to create a closer, while more comfy shave and somehow EJ just seems to work REAL WELL with the sharper blades like Feather (infact Feather is specficially mentioned as a blade that works and feels REAL GOOD with the EJ razor).  Given that I have narrowed down my favorite blades to the mild and universally considered \\&quot;sweet spot\\&quot; Astra blades and \\&quot;sharpest in the industry/clinically sharp\\&quot; Feather blades.  I think that EJ feels comfortable and gives a nice smooth/close shave with both blades is a strong testament to that.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So.. winner EJ.  Its&#x27; far more forgiving.  It actually gives a closer shave on top of that (rare to hear both).  Seems to be compatible and work extra well with multiple different types of blades (be it mild or sharp).  Has the larger/longer handle (although not so good with grip.. but wait.. for my \\&quot;ultimate lessons\\&quot;), and i think is even cheaper now (on Amazon atleast by a few ~ you can get it for $28.. while the merkur i think is in the high 30/low 40s).  Plua it&#x27;s prettier, comes in a super nice box, etc.  It&#x27;s just hard to beat.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;NOW.. \\&quot;ultimate lessons\\&quot;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;firstly on these two razors.  I recommend getting a 3-piece razor over a 2-piece razor (which is why I say if you like and want to try Merkur, get the classic safety razor instead of the 34c... the 34c is a 2-piece, the classic safety is a 30piece).  With 3 piece razors you can mix/match heads, holders, handles from any brand and mix them up to customize a razor exactly the way you like it.  This saves you some money as anything you buy you can use and swap with 3-pieces, not so with 2-pieces or butterfly heads (which are 1-piece).  dont&#x27; like the handle of the EJ de89 (most don&#x27;t.. ) not a problem - just get a new handle you like and you can still enjoy the benefits of the ej de89 razor head/holder.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Next.. what&#x27;s more important in yoru shave experience and performance is prepping your face well and the cr&amp;egrave;me/soap you buy to lather with.  And what you want to look for... is long lasting, and re-activating SLICKNESS ~ one that doen&#x27;t quickly dry up whie you shave.  The razor \\&quot;glide\\&quot; on your face is everything - so focus on SLICK (most people will just review based on latherability, richness, and smell - enh.. not helpful in the end).  Let&#x27;s face it.. we&#x27;re here to shave.. so how it comes off with the razor is really what&#x27;s important (not how it goes on!).  The best product i&#x27;ve found so far.. which i recommend you get , available locally in drugstores, is Cremo Cr&amp;egrave;me.  Its super slick, don&#x27;t need to lather, and re-activates with water.  By far the most comfy, smoothest, \\&quot;glidiest\\&quot; shave.  But I&#x27;m continuing my search now with soaps (figure they&#x27;re slicker than cr&amp;egrave;mes in general).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;OH... brush.. Badger?  Boar?  Synthetic?  To beginners I would say get a synthetic until you learn more, get more experience, become more acquainted with what you like and brand names and reputations so you can hone in on the exact brush you want and why.  Can&#x27;t go wrong with a Synthetic until you can find better elsewhere. (they clean easier, dry faster, are soft, don&#x27;t shed as much, don&#x27;t smell, and cheaper.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Happy Shaving and have fun....joy the benefits of the ej de89 razor head/holder.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Next.. what&#x27;s more important in yoru shave experience and performance is prepping your face well and the crème/soap you buy to lather with.  And what you want to look for... is long lasting, and re-activating SLICKNESS ~ one that doen&#x27;t quickly dry up whie you shave.  The razor \\&quot;glide\\&quot; on your face is everything - so focus on SLICK (most people will just review based on latherability, richness, and smell - enh.. not helpful in the end).     <li> This razor has given me the best shave of my life. And I&#x27;ve had the best shave of my life.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve been shaving since age 13. I have used either disposables, starting with the single edge Bic razors (the yellow/orange ones that look like their cheap ballpoint pens) and moving to most recently the Shick ST2 disposables. I&#x27;ve never used the swivel heads. With disposables, I&#x27;ve gotten maybe one good shave, and the rest of the time its like dragging a dull butter knife across my face. Even so, many times I have thrown out a disposable razor just from the start as too dull or nicked fresh out of the bag, for shaving. Sometimes two or three in a row.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have used electric razors, never ever gotten a good shave or had one last either beyond a few months.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I can&#x27;t understand why I did not switch to this safety razor years ago! Leave aside cost, this is the best shave of my life!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have sensitive skin, and have been shaving in the shower with the Schick ST2s and Barbasol shaving cream, usually cutting myself good every other day too.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My first shave, I cut myself (mildly) on the upper lip being too aggressive, since then no problems.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I am down to two passes, one with the grain, and then against. I had to do three passes or more, sometimes five, with the Schick disposables.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My set up: The Edwin Jagger De89lbl (you want this one because the vertical lines on the chrome handle provide extra grip, the other models are smooth). The included Derby razor blades, still on the first one. I bought the Van Der Hagen brush kit, including soap and mug, at a local place, but you can get the deluxe or cheap version here at Amazon for competitive prices.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I shower, wash my face, shampoo, rinse off the shampoo and put on conditioner. Then, having soaked my brush inhot water in a mug while showering, I whip up lather with the brush and soap in the included shaving kit from Van Der Hagen, getting stiff peaks like whipping egg whites and its pretty easy -- takes maybe two minutes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Shave with the grain and then against, maybe a pass on a few minor areas that need touch up (I go by feel).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Tip: if you cut yourself go back into the shower, for a few minutes, that usually stops the bleeding. I then rinse off the razor, dry it, and put everything away. Put on some aftershave and you are done, total time including shower and shave is about 30 min. Not bad either.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you are transitioning from disposable razors especially if you have not used the stupid swivel heads you are good to go.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A few other tips: choke up on the razor like a chef&#x27;s knife when you are doing detail cutting. The shorter handle than the plastic disposables really does not make much difference, because you are going to be very gentle and using a choke grip for greater control. The weight of the razor will give you all the cutting power you need, unlike plastic disposables.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;EJ recommends that you loosen the razor handle so the blade is not bent after shaving, I put mine in the medicine cabinet and use the shelf to loosen and tighten the handle, not touching the head of the razor.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;When putting in a new razor blade or changing, I do it before I step into the shower when the razor is bone dry, and use (I saw this in Youtube videos) a sandwich approach with thumb and forefinger on the short, non-razor blade edge side, to keep them together. I&#x27;ve seen other videos where a guy puts a towel down on the sink and uses the towel to stabilize the razor heads and does not even touch the head. I have not tried it but seems straight forward.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I would recommend a variety pack of blades, part of the fun of this razor is trying different kinds of blades. That&#x27;s the point of a safety razor, you can have all sorts of different blades for dirt cheap and get the shave you want, it is endlessly customizable.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is my third shave with this razor and coming from disposables, I find it very similar to use, just nicer in every way. I plan on shaving one more time with this razor blade, then before shaving (again when the razor is dry) cleaning the whole thing with anti-bacterial soap, a toothbrush, and hot water. You don&#x27;t want to use bleach or vinegar because it will take off the chrome, keep it simple.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The bottom line on this razor is that you WILL save money, but the biggest advantage is the closest, least aggravating, smoothest shave you&#x27;ll ever have in your life. I already have the smoothest skin on my face after a shave. It is Baby Bare Bottom smooth.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Final caveat: the head is made of some zinc alloy, so don&#x27;t drop it. Yes you can get comparable vintage razors with stainless heads, you&#x27;ll pay a LOT more for them and they won&#x27;t be new either.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I cannot recommend this highly enough. The razor will give you the best shave of your life.</li>

After shaving with the 23C I can re-shave with my favorite Gillett and take off more whiskers for that infamous \\&quot;baby bottom smooth\\&quot; shave.  I just can&#x27;t get that with the Merkur.  That made me curious. That curiosity led me to buying another razor called a Maggard (an internet search will take you to the Maggard site if you&#x27;re interested ... there are also a few good videos on Utube as well).  I bought a Maggard MR18 (for $15.95 no less) and found that it did provide a shave that is the equal to my favorite Gillett ... and in some ways better).  On the Maggard site I learned that the Maggard has the same blade gap as the Edwin Jagger (0.030 inches).  After investigating the Jagger I bought the Edwin Jagger DE89Lbl.  And there is no getting around it ... the Edwin Jagger is a most beautiful razor.  But I discovered that while it provided a closer shave than the Merkur ... it really didn&#x27;t quite match the shave I get with the Maggard ... not quite.  Why I wondered?  That question led me to the realization that what you really find on most sites is people&#x27;s opinions ... and that&#x27;s all  ... but nothing based on measurable facts.  And I realized that the manufacturers seem negligent in providing design type information (other than size and weight information ... excepy the Maggard site states info on blade gap).  That led me to realize that a razor is the result of a design process where a manufacturer constructs his razor based on certain parameters.  The question is ... what are those parameters?  Obviously two of them are blade gap and weight. For those who would like to know a bit about this read on:&lt;br /&gt;The aggressiveness of a razor largely relies on 5 different factors.&lt;br /&gt;  Blade gap&lt;br /&gt;  exposure&lt;br /&gt;  Blade angle in the razor&lt;br /&gt;  Razor weight&lt;br /&gt;  Distribution of the weight. (Heavy head/light handle vs. all heavy.)&lt;br /&gt;  Blade angle applied by the user&lt;br /&gt;The most important factors appear to be blade gap, exposure, and weight.&lt;br /&gt;The greater the blade gap the more aggressive.  The greater the exposure the more aggressive.  The greater the weight the more aggressive.&lt;br /&gt;The Maggard and the Edwin Jagger both have blade gaps of 0.030 inches.  What I discovered is that the Merkur 23C has a blade gap of only 0.025 inches (so blade gap wise its less aggressive and so isn&#x27;t as likely to provide as close a shave as the EJ or the Maggard).  Just FYI ... the Merkur 34C has a blade gap of 0.028 inches ... so it will likely be more aggressive than the 23C but not as aggressive ... and therefore not give as close a shave ... as the EJ or the Maggard.  I won&#x27;t discuss the razor weights here as that&#x27;s information easily found.  Information on blade exposure is almost impossible to find.  I wondered why the Maggard gave me a closer shave than the EJ.  I found what I consider to be the reason.  A three piece razor has a razor head made of two parts ... the cap and the base (where the safety bar constitutes part of the base). I found that the EJ cap and the Merkur23C cap have what appears to be exactly the same width (standing them side by side).  So the primary difference in the two is the blade gap ... and that appears to constitute the primary reason why the EJ provides a closer shave than the Merkur (and its a bit heavier as well I believe).  However ... the Maggard&#x27;s cap is not quite as wide as the EJ and Merkur caps.  This means the blade is a bit more exposed on the Maggard than it is on either the EJ or the Merkur.  And I think this is the reason it provides a closer shave than either the EJ or the Merkur ... it has a bit greater blade exposure ... and its heavier than either the Merkur or EJ.&lt;br /&gt;Anyway ... these are some of the things I&#x27;ve learned in my researching and I hope they help you in your search for the perfect razor.&lt;br /&gt;With that said ... I still will say that I am still pleased to own the Edwin Jagger as it is an exquisite thing of beauty ... something anyone would be proud to own.  But the fact is ... the razor I shave with now actually is the $15.95 Maggard.  And actually ... if one is not adverse to buying a Maggard that has some cosmetic imperfections he can buy such for $10.95!  In fact I just bought a couple of these for my sons.  Happy shaving ... and \\&quot;shave on\\&quot;!</li>
    <li> You are probably reading this because you&#x27;re like the majority of everyone who&#x27;s reviewed this razor... you&#x27;ve had enough...     <li> I don&#x27;t like spending my money if I don&#x27;t have to.  More than that, I prefer function over form. From this we can identify the razor as a DE89L and see that the screw thread remains in the handle.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It is not always clear why a head may shear, often it is due to over-tightening or being dropped. If the screw post is embedded in the handle, some of our razors can be returned for repair as we are able to remove the post and affix a new head. However with your razor this is not feasible so we will need to replace the razor for you.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Please confirm your delivery address and we will arrange for a replacement to be sent to you.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;We hope to hear from you soon.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Kind regards,&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Repairs Department - KC&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Edwin Jagger Ltd.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;www.edwinjagger.com&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;www.facebook.com/edwinjagger&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Their razors may not be built sturdy, but their customer service is top notch.     <li> I have no nostalgic feelings toward wet shaving, but I started looking into it because, on a lark, I happened to click on an Amazon product recommendation for wet shave cream. Since regular cartridge shaving is a irritating (literally) and expensive, I figured why not give it a try.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I did my research, and I was surprised to see how passionate some people are about wet shaving. I was skeptical that it would be the life changing experience that some enthusiast seem to claim, but I went ahead and bought a best badger brush, some VDH soap, and this razor. Nothing ventured, nothing gained.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ll try to update my review periodically and let you know how I feel about it as I get more comfortable with it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;FIRST SHAVE 1/19/13&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Upon un-boxing the razor, I was struck by how nice this thing looked. The entire thing is very shiny like a watch or a nice piece of jewelry, and the design is sort of utilitarian/ turn of the century chic. It really is a display piece. It&#x27;s pretty short, about 2/3 the length of my mach3, and it has a nice heft to it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Adding a blade was easy. Just unscrew the handle, sandwich a blade between the two head pieces, and then screw the handle back on. Voila.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One cheek into the shave I thought \\&quot;meh, this is really no different than cartridge shaving\\&quot;. But then I realized that it&#x27;s no different than cartridge shaving, but at 1/10 the cost of a cartridge. In about 2 months, the razor will have paid for itself, and I will be on track to save about $200 per year on blades. Solid win.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After the shave was when I noticed the difference in the quality of the shave. My shave was rather uneven due to my lack of experience using the razor. The close parts were much closer than I would normally have gotten with my mach3. Those parts of my face felt really nice. Really, really nice. The other parts were slightly worse than what I would have gotten with my mach3. I had some trouble finding the proper angle for tricky areas like my chin. It was pretty clear that once I get used to using the razor on the more tricky parts of my face, I should be able to get a very good shave all around.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I was a skeptic at first, but I can see why experienced wet shavers say that you can get the best shave of your life with this type of set up. The only con, I can think of right now is that the razor is a little slippery when wet and I got a little hand fatigue from trying to maintain a secure grip. No biggie though.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Oh yeah, the soap and brush didn&#x27;t work so well for me. There&#x27;s clearly a proper soap to water ratio that I&#x27;m missing, and I am probably lacking some finer point of technique. I&#x27;m not very interested in becoming a later making expert, so I&#x27;m going to try it with another type of soap or maybe a cream. But if that doesn&#x27;t work,then I may just switch back to the canned stuff.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE 2/10/13&lt;br /&gt;It really is true what they say that finding the combination of products is crucial to having a good shave experience. I think that I&#x27;ve now found my own shave nirvana with this razor, feather blades, and a couple of different creams. That, combined with the right shave technique to bring it all together, and I am now a convert.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I was contemplating buying a Merkur HD so I could have a slightly more aggressive razor as a back up, but now I feel no need to tinker with current set up.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE 3/16/13&lt;br /&gt;I had to travel for a week, and I brought my Mach3 with me since TSA rules are vague regarding DE razor blades. Wow, what a reminder of how bad disposable cartridges are! My Edwin Jagger is clearly a better shaver all around. The blades last longer, the shave is closer, and it&#x27;s so much cheaper. I wish that I had discovered wet shaving years ago. I shave everyday now, and I actually enjoy doing it as well. I could never had said that about shaving with my disposables.     <li> This is an excellent razor. Perfectly crafted, it looks slick. I&#x27;m glad I went with this &amp;#34;lined detail&amp;#34; model rather than the smooth chrome model. It&#x27;s balanced exactly the same and gives a little more grip to the handle. It even looks classier, in my opinion.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Speaking of balance, this razor is perfectly weighted. It&#x27;s not too heavy, but with a good blade you won&#x27;t feel the need to press against your face, which is a no-no anyway. I&#x27;d say it&#x27;s ideal for medium-sharp to very-sharp blades. So, not the Derby blades that come with it. They&#x27;re really dull, and you&#x27;re going to want to try some other blades. I&#x27;ve listed three good alternatives below.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After talking with some friends who have used butterfly-opening razors, I&#x27;m really glad I went for this one instead. It opens easily by unscrewing the handle, which releases from the top two sections, leaving three total chromed pieces and your blade. Simple, elegant, easy to use, and easy to clean.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m using Edwin Jagger&#x27;s Best Badger brush, Edwin Jagger Traditional Shaving Soap (Sandalwood), and Proraso Liquid After Shave Cream (the white stuff, balm-like with no alcohol). I shave down, then angled above the chin, then up, rinsing and lathering between each step. My hair is straight and thick, my skin is medium-fair, and my neck is relatively sensitive.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here is my review of the blades I&#x27;ve tried. There are a lot of sampler packs on Amazon, but after doing some research I chose to order around 30 each of just a few different blades to try, avoiding all of the lesser-quality &amp;#34;filler&amp;#34;. I&#x27;ll compare here and there to Mach-3 blades since that&#x27;s what I previously used before switching to electric, and now this.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;First off, Derby is what is pictured at the time of this review and is what came with my razor. These you can practically rake across your face any way you see fit. They aren&#x27;t very sharp, on par with a Mach-3 that&#x27;s been used a few times. Shaving requires more strokes which leads to more irritation, especially on the neck. That said, I&#x27;d say these are a good blade if you&#x27;re super worried about cutting yourself, because it&#x27;s practically impossible. But even beginners might want to look elsewhere as these blades kind of ruin the &amp;#34;shaving experience&amp;#34;. Don&#x27;t be disappointed if you just bought this razor and have only tried these blades! Keep reading...&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I ordered a 100-pack of Astra SP Platinum (that&#x27;s Astra Superior Premium Platinum, not the regular stainless) since it&#x27;s under ten bucks at the time of this writing. These are great. Beginners, start here. They&#x27;re sharp enough that you don&#x27;t have to press the razor against your skin—which you shouldn&#x27;t have to! You&#x27;re supposed to let the weight of your razor do the work as you guide it along your face in short strokes. So naturally, these are sharper than Mach-3 blades, but if you do press a little, you probably won&#x27;t nick yourself. I love these blades because for me, they&#x27;re comfortable enough for everyday use and provide good, close shaves at a very inexpensive price. Easy on my neck with care. My go-to blade. Great for beginners and pros alike, and eligible for Subscribe &amp; Save!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Wilkinson Sword Classic seem to be great blades for people who have their technique down pretty well. Compared to Astra SP Platinum, they are sharper. They provided the best shave of the lot, but I did nick myself here and there on my neck and below my chin the first time around. Do not push these blades against your skin. It doesn&#x27;t take much mastery to use these, and they&#x27;re worth working up to. Downside: more than twice the price of Astra SP Platinum. I&#x27;ll keep some of these around for days when I want the closest shave possible, or I just feel like something different. If you&#x27;re new to traditional shaving or think Mach-3 blades are sharp, maybe don&#x27;t start here, but definitely try them out.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Feather &amp;#34;New Hi Stainless&amp;#34; Platinum Coated blades are exactly what the reviews say: sharp. My first shave I got a good amount of nicks, but my second I had almost none. I adapted well, and you have to; each brand is a little different and the best require good technique, but some are more forgiving than others. These are negligibly sharper than the Wilkinson Sword Classic but they aren&#x27;t forgiving at all and I didn&#x27;t achieve any better of a shave. They&#x27;re incredibly sharp compared to a Mach-3 blade. At 2x the price of the aforementioned and more than 3x the price of Astra SP Platinum, I won&#x27;t be keeping these on hand, but your mileage may vary. If you only want the sharpest blade around, this is it. Fun fact: these come ten to a pack instead of five.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In conclusion, I&#x27;m sticking with Astra SP Platinum for regular use and Wilkinson Sword Classic when I&#x27;m up for something sharper. I shave every other day, and either is priced reasonably enough that if I want, I can use each side of a blade just once for a fresh edge every shave. That&#x27;s about a 100-pack every year, so do the maths on price. Of course, both brands last much longer than this if you&#x27;re looking for even better value.s are exactly what the reviews say: sharp.
